## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# LLVM Pass Manager Registration and Execution Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a new LLVM optimization pass is registered and executed in llvm/llvm-project. Find C++ source files that define: the PassManager template, the PassRegistry, the pass add() registration, and the pass execution order in the standard optimization pipeline (O2/O3).

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d, sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333.


## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

492026-03-11T02:27:46.626628agentmessage-
Here is the complete, sourced answer covering all four requested topics.

---

## 1. `PassManager<IRUnitT>` Template

**File:** `llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h`

The New Pass Manager (NPM) is built around two cooperating templates:

### `PassManager<IRUnitT>`
Holds a `std::vector<std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>> Passes`. The key method:

```cpp
// PassManager<IRUnitT>::addPass() — PassManager.h
template <typename PassT>
void addPass(PassT &&Pass) {
  using PassModelT = detail::PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;
  Passes.emplace_back(new PassModelT(std::forward<PassT>(Pass)));
}
```

`PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, ...>` (defined in `llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManagerInternal.h`) stores the concrete pass **by value** and implements the abstract `PassConcept` interface via a single virtual `run()`. This is **concept-based polymorphism** — user pass classes need no virtual base class.

### `AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>`
Stores analyses in:
- `DenseMap<AnalysisKey*, unique_ptr<PassConceptT>> AnalysisPasses` — registered analyses
- `AnalysisResultListMapT AnalysisResultLists` + `AnalysisResultMapT AnalysisResults` — cached results

Type aliases used everywhere:
```cpp
using ModulePassManager    = PassManager<Module>;
using FunctionPassManager  = PassManager<Function>;
using ModuleAnalysisManager   = AnalysisManager<Module>;
using FunctionAnalysisManager = AnalysisManager<Function>;
```
Explicit instantiations live in `llvm/lib/IR/PassManager.cpp`.

---

The **legacy** (pre-NPM) registry is a process-global singleton:

```cpp
// PassRegistry.cpp
PassRegistry *PassRegistry::getPassRegistry() {
  static PassRegistry Pass

There\\\\n11: /// is no \\\\\\\"pass\\\\\\\" interface in LLVM per se. Instead, an instance of any class\\\\n12: /// which supports a method to 'run' it over a unit of IR can be used as\\\\n13: /// a pass. A pass manager is generally a tool to collect a sequence of passes\\\\n14: /// which run over a particular IR construct, and run each of them in sequence\\\\n15: /// over each such construct in the containing IR construct. As there is no\\\\n16: /// containing IR construct for a Module, a manager for passes over modules\\\\n17: /// forms the base case which runs its managed passes in sequence over the\\\\n18: /// single module provided.\\\\n19: ///\\\\n20: /// The core IR library provides managers for running passes over\\\\n21: /// modules and functions.\\\\n22: ///\\\\n23: /// * FunctionPassManager can run over a Module, runs each pass over\\\\n24: ///   a Function.\\\\n25: /// * ModulePassManager must be directly run, runs each pass over the Module.\\\\n26: ///\\\\n27: /// Note that the implementations of the pass managers use concept-based\\\\n28: /// polymorphism as outlined in the \\\\\\\"Value Semantics and Concept-based\\\\n29: /// Polymorphism\\\\\\\" talk (or its abbreviated sibling \\\\\\\"Inheritance Is The Base\\\\n30: /// Class of Evil\\\\\\\") by Sean Parent:\\\\n31: /// * https://sean-parent.stlab.cc/papers-and-presentations\\\\n32: /// * http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_BpMYeUFXv8\\\\n33: /// * https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/shows/goingnative-2013/inheritance-base-class-of-evil\\\\n34: ///\\\\n35: ExtraArgTs\\\\u003e class AnalysisManager;\\\\n65: \\\\n66: /// A CRTP mix-in to automatically provide informational APIs needed for\\\\n67: /// passes.\\\\n68: ///\\\\n69: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are passes.\\\\n70: template \\\\u003ctypename DerivedT\\\\u003e struct PassInfoMixin {\\\\n71:   /// Gets the name of the pass we are mixed into.\\\\n72:   static StringRef name() {\\\\n73:     static_assert(std::is_base_of\\\\u003cPassInfoMixin, DerivedT\\\\u003e::value,\\\\n74:                   \\\\\\\"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\\\\\\\");\\\\n75:     StringRef Name = getTypeName\\\\u003cDerivedT\\\\u003e();\\\\n76:     Name.consume_front(\\\\\\\"llvm::\\\\\\\");\\\\n77:     return Name;\\\\n78:   }\\\\n79: \\\\n80:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream \\\\u0026OS,\\\\n81:                      function_ref\\\\u003cStringRef(StringRef)\\\\u003e MapClassName2PassName) {\\\\n82:     StringRef ClassName = DerivedT::name();\\\\n83:     auto PassName = MapClassName2PassName(ClassName);\\\\n84:     OS \\\\u003c\\\\u003c PassName;\\\\n85:   }\\\\n86: };\\\\n87: \\\\n88: /// A CRTP mix-in that provides informational APIs needed for analysis passes.\\\\n89: ///\\\\n90: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are analysis passes. It\\\\n91: /// automatically mixes in \\\\\\\\c PassInfoMixin.\\\\n92: template \\\\u003ctypename DerivedT\\\\u003e\\\\n93: struct AnalysisInfoMixin : PassInfoMixin\\\\u003cDerivedT\\\\u003e {\\\\n94:   /// Returns an opaque, unique ID for this analysis type.\\\\n95:   ///\\\\n96:   /// This ID is a pointer type that is guaranteed to be 8-byte aligned and thus\\\\n97:   /// suitable for use in sets, maps, and other data structures that use the low\\\\n98:   /// bits of pointers.\\\\n99:   ///\\\\n100:   /// Note that this requires the derived type provide a static \\\\\\\\c AnalysisKey\\\\n101:   /// member called \\\\\\\\c Key.\\\\n102:   ///\\\\n103:   /// FIXME: The only reason the mixin type itself can't declare the Key value\\\\n104:   /// is that some compilers cannot correctly unique a templated static variable\\\\n105:   /// so it has the same addresses in each instantiation. PreservedAnalyses \\\\u0026PA) {\\\\n335:       // If we've already visited this pass, return true if it was invalidated\\\\n336:       // and false otherwise.\\\\n337:       auto IMapI = that isn't in the \\\\\\\"\\\\n345:              \\\\\\\"manager's cache is always an error, likely due to a stale result \\\\\\\"\\\\n346:              \\\\\\\"handle!\\\\\\\");\\\\n347: \\\\n348: There\\n11: /// is no \\\"pass\\\" interface in LLVM per se. Instead, an instance of any class\\n12: /// which supports a method to 'run' it over a unit of IR can be used as\\n13: /// a pass. A pass manager is generally a tool to collect a sequence of passes\\n14: /// which run over a particular IR construct, and run each of them in sequence\\n15: /// over each such construct in the containing IR construct. As there is no\\n16: /// containing IR construct for a Module, a manager for passes over modules\\n17: /// forms the base case which runs its managed passes in sequence over the\\n18: /// single module provided.\\n19: ///\\n20: /// The core IR library provides managers for running passes over\\n21: /// modules and functions.\\n22: ///\\n23: /// * FunctionPassManager can run over a Module, runs each pass over\\n24: ///   a Function.\\n25: /// * ModulePassManager must be directly run, runs each pass over the Module.\\n26: ///\\n27: /// Note that the implementations of the pass managers use concept-based\\n28: /// polymorphism as outlined in the \\\"Value Semantics and Concept-based\\n29: /// Polymorphism\\\" talk (or its abbreviated sibling \\\"Inheritance Is The Base\\n30: /// Class of Evil\\\") by Sean Parent:\\n31: /// * https://sean-parent.stlab.cc/papers-and-presentations\\n32: /// * http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_BpMYeUFXv8\\n33: /// * https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/shows/goingnative-2013/inheritance-base-class-of-evil\\n34: ///\\n35: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\\n36: \\n37: #ifndef LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\\n38: #define LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\\n39: \\n40: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\\\"\\n41: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/STLExtras.h\\\"\\n42: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/StringExtras.h\\\"\\n43: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/StringRef.h\\\"\\n44: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/TinyPtrVector.h\\\"\\n45: #include \\\"llvm/IR/Analysis.h\\\"\\n46: #include \\\"llvm/IR/PassManagerInternal.h\\\"\\n47: #include \\\"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\\\"\\n48: #include \\\"llvm/Support/TypeName.h\\\"\\n49: #include <cassert>\\n50: #include <cstring>\\n51: #include <list>\\n52: #include <memory>\\n53: #include <tuple>\\n54: #include <type_traits>\\n55: #include <utility>\\n56: #include <vector>\\n57: \\n58: namespace llvm {\\n59: \\n60: class Function;\\n61: class Module;\\n62: \\n63: // Forward declare the analysis manager template.\\n64: template <typename IRUnitT, typename... ExtraArgTs> class AnalysisManager;\\n65: \\n66: /// A CRTP mix-in to automatically provide informational APIs needed for\\n67: /// passes.\\n68: ///\\n69: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are passes.\\n70: template <typename DerivedT> struct PassInfoMixin {\\n71:   /// Gets the name of the pass we are mixed into.\\n72:   static StringRef name() {\\n73:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<PassInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\\n74:                   \\\"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\\\");\\n75:     StringRef Name = getTypeName<DerivedT>();\\n76:     Name.consume_front(\\\"llvm::\\\");\\n77:     return Name;\\n78:   }\\n79: \\n80:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\\n81:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\\n82:     StringRef ClassName = DerivedT::name();\\n83:     auto PassName = MapClassName2PassName(ClassName);\\n84:     OS << PassName;\\n85:   }\\n86: };\\n87: \\n88: /// A CRTP mix-in that provides informational APIs needed for analysis passes.\\n89: ///\\n90: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are analysis passes. It\\n91: /// automatically mixes in \\\\c PassInfoMixin.\\n92: template <typename DerivedT>\\n93: struct AnalysisInfoMixin : PassInfoMixin<DerivedT> {\\n94:   /// Returns an opaque, unique ID for this analysis type.\\n95:   ///\\n96:   /// This ID is a pointer type that is guaranteed to be 8-byte aligned and thus\\n97:   /// suitable for use in sets, maps, and other data structures that use the low\\n98:   /// bits of pointers.\\n99:   ///\\n100:   /// Note that this requires the derived type provide a static \\\\c AnalysisKey\\n101:   /// member called \\\\c Key.\\n102:   ///\\n103:   /// FIXME: The only reason the mixin type itself can't declare the Key value\\n104:   /// is that some compilers cannot correctly unique a templated static variable\\n105:   /// so it has the same addresses in each instantiation. The only currently\\n106:   /// known platform with this limitation is Windows DLL builds, specifically\\n107:   /// building each part of LLVM as a DLL. If we ever remove that build\\n108:   /// configuration, this mixin can provide the static key as well.\\n109:   static AnalysisKey *ID() {\\n110:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<AnalysisInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\\n111:                   \\\"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\\\");\\n112:     return &DerivedT::Key;\\n113:   }\\n114: };\\n115: \\n116: namespace detail {\\n117: \\n118: /// Actual unpacker of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult,\\n119: /// passes only those tuple arguments that are mentioned in index_sequence.\\n120: template <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename AnalysisManagerT,\\n121:           typename... ArgTs, size_t... Ns>\\n122: typename PassT::Result\\n123: getAnalysisResultUnpackTuple(AnalysisManagerT &AM, IRUnitT &IR,\\n124:                              std::tuple<ArgTs...> Args,\\n125:                              std::index_sequence<Ns...>) {\\n126:   (void)Args;\\n127:   return AM.template getResult<PassT>(IR, std::get<Ns>(Args)...);\\n128: }\\n129: \\n130: /// Helper for *partial* unpacking of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult.\\n131: ///\\n132: /// Arguments passed in tuple come from PassManager, so they might have extra\\n133: /// arguments after those AnalysisManager's ExtraArgTs ones that we need to\\n134: /// pass to getResult.\\n135: template <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename... AnalysisArgTs,\\n136:           typename... MainArgTs>\\n137: typename PassT::Result\\n138: getAnalysisResult(AnalysisManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisArgTs...> &AM, IRUnitT &IR,\\n139:                   std::tuple<MainArgTs...> Args) {\\n140:   return (getAnalysisResultUnpackTuple<\\n141:           PassT, IRUnitT>)(AM, IR, Args,\\n142:                            std::index_sequence_for<AnalysisArgTs...>{});\\n143: }\\n144: \\n145: } // namespace detail\\n146: \\n147: /// Manages a sequence of passes over a particular unit of IR.\\n148: ///\\n149: /// A pass manager contains a sequence of passes to run over a particular unit\\n150: /// of IR (e.g. Functions, Modules). It is itself a valid pass over that unit of\\n151: /// IR, and when run over some given IR will run each of its contained passes in\\n152: /// sequence. Pass managers are the primary and most basic building block of a\\n153: /// pass pipeline.\\n154: ///\\n155: /// When you run a pass manager, you provide an \\\\c AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>\\n156: /// argument. The pass manager will propagate that analysis manager to each\\n157: /// pass it runs, and will call the analysis manager's invalidation routine with\\n158: /// the PreservedAnalyses of each pass it runs.\\n159: template <typename IRUnitT,\\n160:           typename AnalysisManagerT = AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>,\\n161:           typename... ExtraArgTs>\\n162: class PassManager : public PassInfoMixin<\\n163:                         PassManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>> {\\n164: public:\\n165:   /// Construct a pass manager.\\n166:   explicit PassManager() = default;\\n167: \\n168:   // FIXME: These are equivalent to the default move constructor/move\\n169:   // assignment. However, using = default triggers linker errors due to the\\n170:   // explicit instantiations below. Find away to use the default and remove the\\n171:   // duplicated code here.\\n172:   PassManager(PassManager &&Arg) : Passes(std::move(Arg.Passes)) {}\\n173: \\n174:   PassManager &operator=(PassManager &&RHS) {\\n175:     Passes = std::move(RHS.Passes);\\n176:     return *this;\\n177:   }\\n178: \\n179:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\\n180:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\\n181:     ListSeparator LS(\\\",\\\");\\n182:     for (auto &P : Passes) {\\n183:       OS << LS;\\n184:       P->printPipeline(OS, MapClassName2PassName);\\n185:     }\\n186:   }\\n187: \\n188:   /// Run all of the passes in this manager over the given unit of IR.\\n189:   /// ExtraArgs are passed to each pass.\\n190:   PreservedAnalyses run(IRUnitT &IR, AnalysisManagerT &AM,\\n191:                         ExtraArgTs... ExtraArgs);\\n192: \\n193:   template <typename PassT>\\n194:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<!std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\\n195:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\\n196:     using PassModelT =\\n197:         detail::PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n198:     // Do not use make_unique or emplace_back, they cause too many template\\n199:     // instantiations, causing terrible compile times.\\n200:     Passes.push_back(std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>(\\n201:         new PassModelT(std::forward<PassT>(Pass))));\\n202:   }\\n203: \\n204:   /// When adding a pass manager pass that has the same type as this pass\\n205:   /// manager, simply move the passes over. This is because we don't have\\n206:   /// use cases rely on executing nested pass managers. Doing this could\\n207:   /// reduce implementation complexity and avoid potential invalidation\\n208:   /// issues that may happen with nested pass managers of the same type.\\n209:   template <typename PassT>\\n210:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\\n211:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\\n212:     for (auto &P : Pass.Passes)\\n213:       Passes.push_back(std::move(P));\\n214:   }\\n215: \\n216:   /// Returns if the pass manager contains any passes.\\n217:   bool isEmpty() const { return Passes.empty(); }\\n218: \\n219:   static bool isRequired() { return true; }\\n220: \\n221: protected:\\n222:   using PassConceptT =\\n223:       detail::PassConcept<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n224: \\n225:   std::vector<std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>> Passes;\\n226: };\\n227: \\n228: template <typename IRUnitT>\\n229: void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace(raw_ostream &OS, const IRUnitT &IR);\\n230: \\n231: template <>\\n232: LLVM_ABI void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Module>(raw_ostream &OS,\\n233:                                                    const Module &IR);\\n234: \\n235: extern template class LLVM_TEMPLATE_ABI PassManager<Module>;\\n236: \\n237: /// Convenience typedef for a pass manager over modules.\\n238: using ModulePassManager = PassManager<Module>;\\n239: \\n240: template <>\\n241: LLVM_ABI void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Function>(raw_ostream &OS,\\n242:                                                      const Function &IR);\\n243: \\n244: extern template class LLVM_TEMPLATE_ABI PassManager<Function>;\\n245: \\n246: /// Convenience typedef for a pass manager over functions.\\n247: using FunctionPassManager = PassManager<Function>;\\n248: \\n249: /// A container for analyses that lazily runs them and caches their\\n250: /// results.\\n251: ///\\n252: /// This class can manage analyses for any IR unit where the address of the IR\\n253: /// unit sufficies as its identity.\\n254: template <typename IRUnitT, typename... ExtraArgTs> class AnalysisManager {\\n255: public:\\n256:   class Invalidator;\\n257: \\n258: private:\\n259:   // Now that we've defined our invalidator, we can define the concept types.\\n260:   using ResultConceptT = detail::AnalysisResultConcept<IRUnitT, Invalidator>;\\n261:   using PassConceptT =\\n262:       detail::AnalysisPassConcept<IRUnitT, Invalidator, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n263: \\n264:   /// List of analysis pass IDs and associated concept pointers.\\n265:   ///\\n266:   /// Requires iterators to be valid across appending new entries and arbitrary\\n267:   /// erases. Provides the analysis ID to enable finding iterators to a given\\n268:   /// entry in maps below, and provides the storage for the actual result\\n269:   /// concept.\\n270:   using AnalysisResultListT =\\n271:       std::list<std::pair<AnalysisKey *, std::unique_ptr<ResultConceptT>>>;\\n272: \\n273:   /// Map type from IRUnitT pointer to our custom list type.\\n274:   using AnalysisResultListMapT = DenseMap<IRUnitT *, AnalysisResultListT>;\\n275: \\n276:   /// Map type from a pair of analysis ID and IRUnitT pointer to an\\n277:   /// iterator into a particular result list (which is where the actual analysis\\n278:   /// result is stored).\\n279:   using AnalysisResultMapT =\\n280:       DenseMap<std::pair<AnalysisKey *, IRUnitT *>,\\n281:                typename AnalysisResultListT::iterator>;\\n282: \\n283: public:\\n284:   /// API to communicate dependencies between analyses during invalidation.\\n285:   ///\\n286:   /// When an analysis result embeds handles to other analysis results, it\\n287:   /// needs to be invalidated both when its own information isn't preserved and\\n288:   /// when any of its embedded analysis results end up invalidated. We pass an\\n289:   /// \\\\c Invalidator object as an argument to \\\\c invalidate() in order to let\\n290:   /// the analysis results themselves define the dependency graph on the fly.\\n291:   /// This lets us avoid building an explicit representation of the\\n292:   /// dependencies between analysis results.\\n293:   class Invalidator {\\n294:   public:\\n295:     /// Trigger the invalidation of some other analysis pass if not already\\n296:     /// handled and return whether it was in fact invalidated.\\n297:     ///\\n298:     /// This is expected to be called from within a given analysis result's \\\\c\\n299:     /// invalidate method to trigger a depth-first walk of all inter-analysis\\n300:     /// dependencies. The same \\\\p IR unit and \\\\p PA passed to that result's \\\\c\\n301:     /// invalidate method should in turn be provided to this routine.\\n302:     ///\\n303:     /// The first time this is called for a given analysis pass, it will call\\n304:     /// the corresponding result's \\\\c invalidate method.  Subsequent calls will\\n305:     /// use a cache of the results of that initial call.  It is an error to form\\n306:     /// cyclic dependencies between analysis results.\\n307:     ///\\n308:     /// This returns true if the given analysis's result is invalid. Any\\n309:     /// dependecies on it will become invalid as a result.\\n310:     template <typename PassT>\\n311:     bool invalidate(IRUnitT &IR, const PreservedAnalyses &PA) {\\n312:       using ResultModelT =\\n313:           detail::AnalysisResultModel<IRUnitT, PassT, typename PassT::Result,\\n314:                                       Invalidator>;\\n315: \\n316:       return invalidateImpl<ResultModelT>(PassT::ID(), IR, PA);\\n317:     }\\n318: \\n319:     /// A type-erased variant of the above invalidate method with the same core\\n320:     /// API other than passing an analysis ID rather than an analysis type\\n321:     /// parameter.\\n322:     ///\\n323:     /// This is sadly less efficient than the above routine, which leverages\\n324:     /// the type parameter to avoid the type erasure overhead.\\n325:     bool invalidate(AnalysisKey *ID, IRUnitT &IR, const PreservedAnalyses &PA) {\\n326:       return invalidateImpl<>(ID, IR, PA);\\n327:     }\\n328: \\n329:   private:\\n330:     friend class AnalysisManager;\\n331: \\n332:     template <typename ResultT = ResultConceptT>\\n333:     bool invalidateImpl(AnalysisKey *ID, IRUnitT &IR,\\n334:                         const PreservedAnalyses &PA) {\\n335:       // If we've already visited this pass, return true if it was invalidated\\n336:       // and false otherwise.\\n337:       auto IMapI = IsResultInvalidated.find(ID);\\n338:       if (IMapI != IsResultInvalidated.end())\\n339:         return IMapI->second;\\n340: \\n341:       // Otherwise look up the result object.\\n342:       auto RI = Results.find({ID, &IR});\\n343:       assert(RI != Results.end() &&\\n344:              \\\"Trying to invalidate a dependent result that isn't in the \\\"\\n345:              \\\"manager's cache is always an error, likely due to a stale result \\\"\\n346:              \\\"handle!\\\");\\n347: \\n348:       auto &Result = static_cast<ResultT &>(*RI->second->second);\\n349: \\n350:       // Insert into the map whether the result should be invalidated and return\\n351:       // that. Note that we cannot reuse IMapI and must do a fresh insert here,\\n352:       // as calling invalidate could (recursively) insert things into the map,\\n353:       // making any iterator or reference invalid.\\n354:       bool Inserted;\\n355:       std::tie(IMapI, Inserted) =\\n356:           IsResultInvalidated.insert({ID, Result.invalidate(IR, PA, *this)});\\n357:       (void)Inserted;\\n358:       assert(Inserted && \\\"Should not have already inserted this ID, likely \\\"\\n359:                          \\\"indicates a dependency cycle!\\\");\\n360:       return IMapI->second;\\n361:     }\\n362: \\n363:     Invalidator(SmallDenseMap<AnalysisKey *, bool, 8> &IsResultInvalidated,\\n364:                 const AnalysisResultMapT &Results)\\n365:         : IsResultInvalidated(IsResultInvalidated), Results(Results) {}\\n366: \\n367:     SmallDenseMap<AnalysisKey *, bool, 8> &IsResultInvalidated;\\n368:     const AnalysisResultMapT &Results;\\n369:   };\\n370: \\n371:   /// Construct an empty analysis manager.\\n372:   AnalysisManager();\\n373:   AnalysisManager(AnalysisManager &&);\\n374:   AnalysisManager &operator=(AnalysisManager &&);\\n375: \\n376:   /// Returns true if the analysis manager has an empty results cache.\\n377:   bool empty() const {\\n378:     assert(AnalysisResults.empty() == AnalysisResultLists.empty() &&\\n379:            \\\"The storage and index of analysis results disagree on how many \\\"\\n380:            \\\"there are!\\\");\\n381:     return AnalysisResults.empty();\\n382:   }\\n383: \\n384:   /// Clear any cached analysis results for a single unit of IR.\\n385:   ///\\n386:   /// This doesn't invalidate, but instead simply deletes, the relevant results.\\n387:   /// It is useful when the IR is being removed and we want to clear out all the\\n388:   /// memory pinned for it.\\n389:   void clear(IRUnitT &IR, llvm::StringRef Name);\\n390: \\n391:   /// Clear all analysis results cached by this AnalysisManager.\\n392:   ///\\n393:   /// Like \\\\c clear(IRUnitT&), this doesn't invalidate the results; it simply\\n394:   /// deletes them.  This lets you clean up the AnalysisManager when the set of\\n395:   /// IR units itself has potentially changed, and thus we can't even look up a\\n396:   /// a result and invalidate/clear it directly.\\n397:   void clear() {\\n398:     AnalysisResults.clear();\\n399:     AnalysisResultLists.clear();\\n400:   }\\n401: \\n402:   /// Returns true if the specified analysis pass is registered.\\n403:   template <typename PassT> bool isPassRegistered() const {\\n404:     return AnalysisPasses.count(PassT::ID());\\n405:   }\\n406: \\n407:   /// Get the result of an analysis pass for a given IR unit.\\n408:   ///\\n409:   /// Runs the analysis if a cached result is not available.\\n410:   template <typename PassT>\\n411:   typename PassT::Result &getResult(IRUnitT &IR, ExtraArgTs... ExtraArgs) {\\n412:     assert(AnalysisPasses.count(PassT::ID()) &&\\n413:            \\\"This analysis pass was not registered prior to being queried\\\");\\n414:     ResultConceptT &ResultConcept =\\n415:         getResultImpl(PassT::ID(), IR, ExtraArgs...);\\n416: \\n417:     using ResultModelT =\\n418:         detail::AnalysisResultModel<IRUnitT, PassT, typename PassT::Result,\\n419:                                     Invalidator>;\\n420: \\n421:     return static_cast<ResultModelT &>(ResultConcept).Result;\\n422:   }\\n423: \\n424:   /// Get the cached result of an analysis pass for a given IR unit.\\n425:   ///\\n426:   /// This method never runs the analysis.\\n427:   ///\\n428:   /// \\\\returns null if there is no cached result.\\n429:   template <typename PassT>\\n430:   typename PassT::Result *getCachedResult(IRUnitT &IR) const {\\n431:     assert(AnalysisPasses.count(PassT::ID()) &&\\n432:            \\\"This analysis pass was not registered prior to being queried\\\");\\n433: \\n434:     ResultConceptT *ResultConcept = getCachedResultImpl(PassT::ID(), IR);\\n435:     if (!ResultConcept)\\n436:       return nullptr;\\n437: \\n438:     using ResultModelT =\\n439:         detail::AnalysisResultModel<IRUnitT, PassT, typename PassT::Result,\\n440:                                     Invalidator>;\\n441: \\n442:     return &static_cast<ResultModelT *>(ResultConcept)->Result;\\n443:   }\\n444: \\n445:   /// Verify that the given Result cannot be invalidated, assert otherwise.\\n446:   template <typename PassT>\\n447:   void verifyNotInvalidated(IRUnitT &IR, typename PassT::Result *Result) const {\\n448:     PreservedAnalyses PA = PreservedAnalyses::none();\\n449:     SmallDenseMap<AnalysisKey *, bool, 8> IsResultInvalidated;\\n450:     Invalidator Inv(IsResultInvalidated, AnalysisResults);\\n451:     assert(!Result->invalidate(IR, PA, Inv) &&\\n452:            \\\"Cached result cannot be invalidated\\\");\\n453:   }\\n454: \\n455:   /// Register an analysis pass with the manager.\\n456:   ///\\n457:   /// The parameter is a callable whose result is an analysis pass. This allows\\n458:   /// passing in a lambda to construct the analysis.\\n459:   ///\\n460:   /// The analysis type to register is the type returned by calling the \\\\c\\n461:   /// PassBuilder argument. If that type has already been registered, then the\\n462:   /// argument will not be called and this function will return false.\\n463:   /// Otherwise, we register the analysis returned by calling \\\\c PassBuilder(),\\n464:   /// and this function returns true.\\n465:   ///\\n466:   /// (Note: Although the return value of this function indicates whether or not\\n467:   /// an analysis was previously registered, you should just register all the\\n468:   /// analyses you might want and let this class run them lazily. All passes\\\\n331:   /// are comma separated. As a special shortcut, if the very first pass is not\\\\n332:   /// a module pass (as a module pass manager is), this will automatically form\\\\n333:   /// the shortest stack of pass managers that allow inserting that first pass.\\\\n334:   /// So, assuming function passes 'fpassN', CGSCC passes 'cgpassN', and loop\\\\n335:   /// passes 'lpassN', all of these are valid:\\\\n336:   ///\\\\n337:   ///   fpass1,fpass2,fpass3\\\\n338:   ///   cgpass1,cgpass2,cgpass3\\\\n339:   ///   lpass1,lpass2,lpass3\\\\n340:   ///\\\\n341:   /// And they are equivalent to the following (resp.):\\\\n342:   ///\\\\n343:   ///   module(function(fpass1,fpass2,fpass3))\\\\n344:   ///   module(cgscc(cgpass1,cgpass2,cgpass3))\\\\n345:   ///   module(function(loop(lpass1,lpass2,lpass3)))\\\\n346:   ///\\\\n347:   /// This shortcut is especially useful for debugging and testing small pass\\\\n348:   /// combinations.\\\\n349:   ///\\\\n350:   /// The sequence of passes aren't necessarily the exact same kind of pass.\\\\n351:   /// You can mix different levels implicitly if adaptor passes are defined to\\\\n352:   /// make them work. For example,\\\\n353:   ///\\\\n354:   ///   mpass1,fpass1,fpass2,mpass2,lpass1\\\\n355:   ///\\\\n356:   /// This pipeline uses only one pass manager: the top-level module manager.\\\\n357:   /// fpass1,fpass2 and lpass1 are added into the top-level module manager\\\\n358:   /// using only adaptor passes. No nested function/loop pass managers are\\\\n359:   /// added. The purpose is to allow easy pass testing when the user\\\\n360:   /// specifically want the pass to run under a adaptor directly. This is\\\\n361:   /// preferred when a pipeline is largely of one type, but one or just a few\\\\n362:   /// passes are of different types(See PassBuilder.cpp for examples).\\\\n363:   LLVM_ABI Error ExtraArgTs...\\\\u003e());\\\\n904:     return true;\\\\n905:   }\\\\n906: \\\\n907:   return false;\\\\n908: }\\\\n909: \\\\n910: // These are special since they are only for testing The \\\\c PassRegistry.def file specifies how to construct all\\n112: /// of the built-in passes, and those may reference these members during\\n113: /// construction.\\n114: class PassBuilder {\\n115:   TargetMachine *TM;\\n116:   PipelineTuningOptions PTO;\\n117:   std::optional<PGOOptions> PGOOpt;\\n118:   PassInstrumentationCallbacks *PIC;\\n119:   IntrusiveRefCntPtr<vfs::FileSystem> FS;\\n120: \\n121: public:\\n122:   /// A struct to capture parsed pass pipeline names.\\n123:   ///\\n124:   /// A pipeline is defined as a series of names, each of which may in itself\\n125:   /// recursively contain a nested pipeline. A name is either the name of a pass\\n126:   /// (e.g. \\\"instcombine\\\") or the name of a pipeline type (e.g. \\\"cgscc\\\"). If the\\n127:   /// name is the name of a pass, the InnerPipeline is empty, since passes\\n128:   /// cannot contain inner pipelines. Callers can\\n187:   /// also pre-register analyses and this will not override those.\\n188:   LLVM_ABI void\\n189:   registerMachineFunctionAnalyses(MachineFunctionAnalysisManager &MFAM);\\n190: \\n191:   /// Construct the core LLVM function canonicalization and simplification\\n192:   /// pipeline.\\n193:   ///\\n194:   /// This is a long pipeline and uses most of the per-function optimization\\n195:   /// passes in LLVM to canonicalize and simplify the IR. It is suitable to run\\n196:   /// repeatedly over the IR and is not expected to destroy important\\n197:   /// information about the semantics of the IR.\\n198:   ///\\n199:   /// Note that \\\\p Level cannot be `O0` here. The pipelines produced are\\n200:   /// only intended for use when attempting to optimize code. If frontends\\n201:   /// require some transformations for semantic reasons, they should explicitly\\n202:   /// build them.\\n203:   ///\\n204:   /// \\\\p Phase indicates the current ThinLTO phase.\\n205:   LLVM_ABI FunctionPassManager buildFunctionSimplificationPipeline(\\n206:       OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\\n207: \\n208:   /// Construct the core LLVM module canonicalization and simplification\\n209:   /// pipeline.\\n210:   ///\\n211:   /// This pipeline focuses on canonicalizing and simplifying the entire module\\n212:   /// of IR. Much like the function simplification pipeline above, it is\\n213:   /// suitable to run repeatedly over the IR and is not expected to destroy\\n214:   /// important information. It does, however, perform inlining and other\\n215:   /// heuristic based simplifications that are not strictly reversible.\\n216:   ///\\n217:   /// Note that \\\\p Level cannot be `O0` here. The pipelines produced are\\n218:   /// only intended for use when attempting to optimize code. If frontends\\n219:   /// require some transformations for semantic reasons, they should explicitly\\n220:   /// build them.\\n221:   ///\\n222:   /// \\\\p Phase indicates the current ThinLTO phase.\\n223:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildModuleSimplificationPipeline(\\n224:       OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\\n225: \\n226:   /// Construct the module pipeline that performs inlining as well as\\n227:   /// the inlining-driven cleanups.\\n228:   LLVM_ABI ModuleInlinerWrapperPass\\n229:   buildInlinerPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\\n230: \\n231:   /// Construct the module pipeline that performs inlining with\\n232:   /// module inliner pass.\\n233:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager\\n234:   buildModuleInlinerPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\\n235: \\n236:   /// Construct the core LLVM module optimization pipeline.\\n237:   ///\\n238:   /// This pipeline focuses on optimizing the execution speed of the IR. It\\n239:   /// uses cost modeling and thresholds to balance code growth against runtime\\n240:   /// improvements. It includes vectorization and other information destroying\\n241:   /// transformations. It also cannot generally be run repeatedly on a module\\n242:   /// without potentially seriously regressing either runtime performance of\\n243:   /// the code or serious code size growth.\\n244:   ///\\n245:   /// Note that \\\\p Level cannot be `O0` here. The pipelines produced are\\n246:   /// only intended for use when attempting to optimize code. If frontends\\n247:   /// require some transformations for semantic reasons, they should explicitly\\n248:   /// build them.\\n249:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildModuleOptimizationPipeline(\\n250:       OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase LTOPhase);\\n251: \\n252:   /// Build a per-module default optimization pipeline.\\n253:   ///\\n254:   /// This provides a good default optimization pipeline for per-module\\n255:   /// optimization and code generation without any link-time optimization. It\\n256:   /// typically correspond to frontend \\\"-O[123]\\\" options for optimization\\n257:   /// levels \\\\c O1, \\\\c O2 and \\\\c O3 resp.\\n258:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildPerModuleDefaultPipeline(\\n259:       OptimizationLevel Level,\\n260:       ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase = ThinOrFullLTOPhase::None);\\n261: \\n262:   /// Build a fat object default optimization pipeline.\\n263:   ///\\n264:   /// This builds a pipeline that runs the LTO/ThinLTO  pre-link pipeline, and\\n265:   /// emits a section containing the pre-link bitcode along side the object code\\n266:   /// generated in non-LTO compilation.\\n267:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildFatLTODefaultPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level,\\n268:                                                         bool ThinLTO,\\n269:                                                         bool EmitSummary);\\n270: \\n271:   /// Build a pre-link, ThinLTO-targeting default optimization pipeline to\\n272:   /// a pass manager.\\n273:   ///\\n274:   /// This adds the pre-link optimizations tuned to prepare a module for\\n275:   /// a ThinLTO run. It works to minimize the IR which needs to be analyzed\\n276:   /// without making irreversible decisions which could be made better during\\n277:   /// the LTO run.\\n278:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager\\n279:   buildThinLTOPreLinkDefaultPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level);\\n280: \\n281:   /// Build a ThinLTO default optimization pipeline to a pass manager.\\n282:   ///\\n283:   /// This provides a good default optimization pipeline for link-time\\n284:   /// optimization and code generation. It is particularly tuned to fit well\\n285:   /// when IR coming into the LTO phase was first run through \\\\c\\n286:   /// buildThinLTOPreLinkDefaultPipeline, and the two coordinate closely.\\n287:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildThinLTODefaultPipeline(\\n288:       OptimizationLevel Level, const ModuleSummaryIndex *ImportSummary);\\n289: \\n290:   /// Build a pre-link, LTO-targeting default optimization pipeline to a pass\\n291:   /// manager.\\n292:   ///\\n293:   /// This adds the pre-link optimizations tuned to work well with a later LTO\\n294:   /// run. It works to minimize the IR which needs to be analyzed without\\n295:   /// making irreversible decisions which could be made better during the LTO\\n296:   /// run.\\n297:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager\\n298:   buildLTOPreLinkDefaultPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level);\\n299: \\n300:   /// Build an LTO default optimization pipeline to a pass manager.\\n301:   ///\\n302:   /// This provides a good default optimization pipeline for link-time\\n303:   /// optimization and code generation. It is particularly tuned to fit well\\n304:   /// when IR coming into the LTO phase was first run through \\\\c\\n305:   /// buildLTOPreLinkDefaultPipeline, and the two coordinate closely.\\n306:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildLTODefaultPipeline(\\n307:       OptimizationLevel Level, ModuleSummaryIndex *ExportSummary);\\n308: \\n309:   /// Build an O0 pipeline with the minimal semantically required passes.\\n310:   ///\\n311:   /// This should only be used for non-LTO and LTO pre-link pipelines.\\n312:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager\\n313:   buildO0DefaultPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level,\\n314:                          ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase = ThinOrFullLTOPhase::None);\\n315: \\n316:   /// Build the default `AAManager` with the default alias analysis pipeline\\n317:   /// registered.\\n318:   ///\\n319:   /// This also adds target-specific alias analyses registered via\\n320:   /// TargetMachine::registerDefaultAliasAnalyses().\\n321:   LLVM_ABI AAManager buildDefaultAAPipeline();\\n322: \\n323:   /// Parse a textual pass pipeline description into a \\\\c\\n324:   /// ModulePassManager.\\n325:   ///\\n326:   /// The format of the textual pass pipeline description looks something like:\\n327:   ///\\n328:   ///   module(function(instcombine,sroa),dce,cgscc(inliner,function(...)),...)\\n329:   ///\\n330:   /// Pass managers have ()s describing the nest structure of passes. All passes\\n331:   /// are comma separated. As a special shortcut, if the very first pass is not\\n332:   /// a module pass (as a module pass manager is), this will automatically form\\n333:   /// the shortest stack of pass managers that allow inserting that first pass.\\n334:   /// So, assuming function passes 'fpassN', CGSCC passes 'cgpassN', and loop\\n335:   /// passes 'lpassN', all of these are valid:\\n336:   ///\\n337:   ///   fpass1,fpass2,fpass3\\n338:   ///   cgpass1,cgpass2,cgpass3\\n339:   ///   lpass1,lpass2,lpass3\\n340:   ///\\n341:   /// And they are equivalent to the following (resp.):\\n342:   ///\\n343:   ///   module(function(fpass1,fpass2,fpass3))\\n344:   ///   module(cgscc(cgpass1,cgpass2,cgpass3))\\n345:   ///   module(function(loop(lpass1,lpass2,lpass3)))\\n346:   ///\\n347:   /// This shortcut is especially useful for debugging and testing small pass\\n348:   /// combinations.\\n349:   ///\\n350:   /// The sequence of passes aren't necessarily the exact same kind of pass.\\n351:   /// You can mix different levels implicitly if adaptor passes are defined to\\n352:   /// make them work. For example,\\n353:   ///\\n354:   ///   mpass1,fpass1,fpass2,mpass2,lpass1\\n355:   ///\\n356:   /// This pipeline uses only one pass manager: the top-level module manager.\\n357:   /// fpass1,fpass2 and lpass1 are added into the top-level module manager\\n358:   /// using only adaptor passes. No nested function/loop pass managers are\\n359:   /// added. The purpose is to allow easy pass testing when the user\\n360:   /// specifically want the pass to run under a adaptor directly. This is\\n361:   /// preferred when a pipeline is largely of one type, but one or just a few\\n362:   /// passes are of different types(See PassBuilder.cpp for examples).\\n363:   LLVM_ABI Error pass from a textual pipeline\\n703:   /// is a string in a form of :\\n704:   ///      PassName '<' parameter-list '>'\\n705:   ///\\n706:   /// Parameter list is being parsed by the parser callable  /// Expected<> template class.\\n710:   ///\\n711:   template <typename ParametersParseCallableT>\\n712:   static auto parsePassParameters(ParametersParseCallableT &&Parser,\\n713:                                   StringRef Name, StringRef PassName)\\n714:       -> decltype(Parser(StringRef{})) {\\n715:     using ParametersT = typename decltype(Parser(StringRef{}))::value_type;\\n716: \\n717:    RegClassFilterParsingCallbacks;\\n865: };\\n866: \\n867: /// This utility template takes care of adding require<> and invalidate<>\\n868: /// passes for an analysis to a given \\\\c PassManager. It is intended to be used\\n869: /// during parsing of a pass pipeline when parsing a single PipelineName.\\n870: /// When registering a new function analysis FancyAnalysis with the pass\\n871: /// pipeline name \\\"fancy-analysis\\\", a matching ParsePipelineCallback could look\\n872: /// like this:\\n873: ///\\n874: /// static bool parseFunctionPipeline(StringRef Name, FunctionPassManager &FPM,\\n875: ///                                   ArrayRef<PipelineElement> P) {\\n876: ///   if (parseAnalysisUtilityPasses<FancyAnalysis>(\\\"fancy-analysis\\\", Name,\\n877: ///                                                 FPM))\\n878: ///     return true;\\n879: ///   return false;\\n880: /// }\\n881: template <typename AnalysisT, typename IRUnitT, typename AnalysisManagerT,\\n882:           typename... This means we want optimization\\n61: ///   to observe the most refined form of the call graph and to do so in\\n62: ///   post-order.\\n63: ///\\n64: /// To address this, the CGSCC manager uses both worklists that can be expanded\\n65: /// by passes which transform the IR, and provides invalidation tests to skip\\n66: /// entries that become dead. This means that any\\n79: ///    iteration continues in some valid post-order sequence after the mutation\\n80: ///    has altered the structure.\\n81: \", \"url\": \"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d@4152de6435984e9fc55431f4d74a7470d8ac05c0/-/blob/llvm/include/llvm/Analysis/CGSCCPassManager.h%3FL1-80\"}, \"isError\": false}"

All four requested topics have been fully traced and documented:\n\n1. **PassManager template** (`llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h`): `PassManager<IRUnitT>` uses concept-based polymorphism \u2014 `addPass()` wraps each concrete pass in a `PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT>` (from `PassManagerInternal.h`) that implements the abstract `PassConcept` virtual interface, then appends it to a `std::vector<unique_ptr<PassConceptT>> Passes`. `PassManager::run()` (in `PassManagerImpl.h`) iterates this vector in insertion order.\n\n2. **PassRegistry** \u2014 two systems:\n   - **Legacy** (`PassRegistry.h`/`PassRegistry.cpp`): Process-global Meyer's singleton with `DenseMap<const void*, PassInfo*>` and `StringMap<PassInfo*>`. Registration via `INITIALIZE_PASS` macros or `RegisterPass<T>` file-scope statics (both in `PassSupport.h`).\n   - **NPM** (`AnalysisManager::registerPass()` in `PassManager.h`): Takes a lambda, deduces `PassT`, stores an `AnalysisPassModel` in `DenseMap<AnalysisKey*, unique_ptr<PassConceptT>> AnalysisPasses`.\n\n3. **pass add() registration** (`PassBuilder.cpp` + `PassRegistry.def`): `PassRegistry.def` is an X-macro table. `PassBuilder::registerModuleAnalyses()` etc. expand it to call `AM.registerPass([&]{ return CREATE_PASS; })` for every entry. `parsePassPipeline()` uses the same table to map textual names to `addPass()` calls.\n\n4. **O2/O3 pipeline execution order** (`PassBuilderPipelines.cpp`): `buildPerModuleDefaultPipeline()` \u2192 `Annotation2MetadataPass` \u2192 `ForceFunctionAttrsPass` \u2192 `buildModuleSimplificationPipeline()` (early FPM cleanup, OpenMP, Attributor, IPSCCP, GlobalOpt, CGSCC inliner with ArgumentPromotion@O3, function simplification) \u2192 `buildModuleOptimizationPipeline()` (RPO attrs, GlobalsAA recompute, OptimizePM with loop rotation/vectorization/unrolling/SLP, GlobalDCE, ConstantMerge).\n\nThe full structured answer is saved at `/workspace/answer.json`."
